One investigator\n\n[17]\n\nobserved that the growth rates of small cracks are slower when\ncompressive residual\n\nstress is present. Other experiments\n\n[27,28] showed that the growth rates of small cracks\npropagating inside of the notch plasticity\nprogressively\n\nuntil\n\nthey arrest\n\ndecrease\n\nor merge with the long crack\n\ncurve.\nAs reviewed above, the anomalous growth behavior of small\ncracks may result\n\nfrom complications due to several mechanical\n\nand metallurgical\n\ncauses, such as crack closure,\n\nplasticity,\n\nand microstructural\n\nTo validate\n\nlocal\n\neffects.\n\nthe existence of the small crack effect,\n\nNASA\n\nhas sponsored a round-robin test program in which 14\nlaboratories\n\nare participating.\n\nIn the study recorded here, as\n\npart of this round-robin program, the growth rates of small\nfatigue cracks from a semi-circular\nthe replica method for different\n\nnotch were measured using\n\nR-ratios.\n\nThe closure behavior\n\nof small cracks was observed for various R-ratios\nstress levels.\n\nand gross\n\nThe closure loads were determined from the load\n\nversus crack opening displacement (COD) data, which were\nobtained using the computer-controlled,\nInterferometric\n\nlaser-based,\n\nStrain/Displacement Gage (ISDG). MeasurementTechniques for Closure in Small Cracks\n\nThe techniques used in measuring the closure behavior of\nlong cracks -- the clip\nthe potential\navailable\n\ngage, the strain\n\ndifference\n\ngage, ultrasonics,\n\nand\n\ntechnique -- generally are not\n\nfor short cracks. Special methods must be applied in\n\nmonitoring small crack closure; these methods must provide\nsufficient\n\nresolution\n\nand be easily adaptable to the shapes and\n\ngeometries of small cracks.\nMorris et al [42] measuredclosure stress on surface\nmicro- cracks with lengths from 70 to 90 microns using scanning\nelectron microscopy (SEM). They measured crack opening\ndisplacement with 30,000X magnification\n\nat each successive load\n\nto take crack compliance data. The crack closure load was\ndetermined from the break point in the linear relationship\nbetween crack opening and applied stress.\n\nJameset al [43] used\n\nthe samemethod as Morris et al [42] in measuring the closure\nload for crack lengths from 600 to 1,000 microns.\nZeiken et al [44] measuredmeanclosure loads on a\nthrough-edge crack with a length of 500 microns using a\nback-face strain\n\ntechnique. This technique developed in another\n\nexperiment [45] determined a closure load from the point where\nthe resulting\n\nelastic\n\ncompliance curves of load versus relative\n\nstrain deviated from linearity.\n\n20\nBreat et al [22] measuredbulk closure load on throughedge cracks with lengths of 300 to 600 microns using a clip\ngage extensometer. Crack closure was determined from a\nP - (_P-_)plot\nlinear\n\nwhere _ was selected in such a way that the\n\npart of the P-_ curve above Pop was vertical.\nSharpe [41] developed a laser-based interferometric\n\ntechnique; Sharpe and Lee [46] described its use in measuring\ncrack opening displacement. His technique has a very short gage\nlength (a few tens of microns) and high resolution\n\n(0.02\n\nmicron). The crack compliance data was obtained from the crack\nopening displacement and closure load was determined by a\n"reduced data method" which is widely used in closure\nmeasurement. Larsen [13] applied a similar\n\ntechnique in\n\nmeasuring the closure load on surface cracks as small as 37\nmicrons.\nWilliams et al [47] developed a stereo-imaging technique\nto monitor the crack tip strain\n\nfield.\n\nThis technique measures\n\ndisplacement with an accuracy of 0.04 micron at 1,000X\nmagnification.\n\nIt can be useful in measuring the behavior of\n\nsmall cracks.\nAll of the preceding techniques have been used to measure\nshort crack closure. However, typical\na notch-mouth clip\n\nbulk techniques, such as\n\ngage or a back-face strain\n\nbe used very carefully\n\ngage (BFS), must\n\nwhen taking surface measurements.\n\n21\nA major problem in the use of compliance methods to\ndetermine the crack-opening point involves the exact position\nof the point at which the compliance is changed, as shown in\nFigure II-i.\n\nJameset al [48] indicate\n\nthat even in long-crack\n\nmeasurements(10-20 mm), when using the BFS(which has about\ntwice the sensitivity\n\nof a notch-mouth clip\n\ncompliance corresponding to the critical\n\ngage) the change in\n\ni00 microns behind the\n\ncrack tip is only on the order of 2%for a/w = 0.4. Such a\nsmall change is extremely difficult\nand the opening point is likely\nresolution\n\nto be underestimated. Better\n\nin determining the crack-opening point can be\n\nobtained by incorporating\ncircuit\n\nto detect experimentally\n\nan offset\n\nelastic\n\ndisplacement\n\ninto the compliance measurementsystem. An offset\n\ndisplacement system is defined as\n_"\n\n= 6 - a P\n\n(2.7)\n\nwhere a is chosen such that 6\' is zero once the crack is fully\nopen. With this method, the detectable crack length can be as\nsmall as 50 microns.\nTechniques involving a SEM laser-based interferometry\nor\nare muchmore useful in measuring the small crack\'s behavior\nbecause they can measurecrack opening displacement directly\nthe crack surface. Then the sensitivity\n\non\n\nin measuring the\n\ndisplacement is very high and the compliance change can be seen\nmore clearly\n\nthan is possible by the bulk technique.\n\n22\n\nLoad\n\na)\n\nCompliance\n\nchange\n\nis shown\n\nat\n\npoint\n\nA\n\nA\n4-J\n\n=\n\nU\n\n4.J\n\no\n\nLoad\n\nb)\n\nOffset\n\nFigure\n\nII-i.\n\ndisplacement\n\ncurve\n\nTypical\n\nload\n\nopening\n\npoint\n\n-\n\ndisplacement\n[48]\n\ncurve\n\nto\n\ndetermine\n\ncrack\n\n23\nIII.\n\nEXPERIMENTAL\nPROCEDURE\n\nIII-I.\n\nMaterials\n\nand Specimens\n\nThe material used in this\n\nstudy was AI 2024-T3, an\n\naluminum alloy which is widely used in the structures\nairplanes.\n\nThe stress-strain\n\nof\n\ndata of this material were found\n\nfor monotonic and cyclic cases as follows\n\n[49].\n\ns = Ee\n\nfor e _\n\ns = K enl\n\nfor el_.e _ e2\n\ns = K en2\n\nfor e > e2\n\nel\n(3.1)\n\nwhere s is the stress in MPa\nE is the elastic modulus in MPa\ne is the strain\nKI and K2 are the material constants in MPa\nnland n2are the power hardening coefficients\n\nThe following values were found for monotonic and cyclic\ncases.\nE\nMonotonic\nCyclic\n\nK1\n\n73100 1013\n73100 5135\n\nK2\n\nel\n\n431\n917\n\n0.0047\n0.0049\n\ne2\n\nnI\n\n0.006 0.2\n0.032\n0.0071 0.499 0.15\n\nThe specimens, which had a stress concentration\n3.17 (detailed\n\nin Appendix I-C),\n\nn2\n\nfactor of\n\nwere supplied by NASA\nLangley\n\nResearch Center and manufactured at Wright-Patterson Air Force\nBase. The crack originated\n\nalong the centerline\n\nroot near the edge of the specimen after\n\nof the notch\n\n120,000 cycles.\n\nReplicas were taken every I0,000 cycles for this test,\nfirst\n\nvisible\n\nso the\n\ncrack was 65 micrometers long before it was\n\nfound. The crack grew toward the center and the edge. Another\ncrack initiated\n\nnear the center of the specimen at 180,000\n\ncycles. A third\n\ncrack appeared at the upper side of the notch\n\nat 210,000 cycles. The first\n\ncrack grew continuously,\n\nbut the\n\nsecond and third cracks stagnated after growing for a short\ntime. Information about crack initiation\n\nand the crack growth\n\nrate behavior can be obtained from the crack maps.\n\n50\nIV-2. Crack Initiation\n\nAnalysis\n\nIt was convenient to examine crack initiation\nthe replicas,\n\neven after the tests were finished.\n\nby observing\nThe smallest\n\nobservable crack was approximately i0 _mlong, viewed under an\noptical\n\nmicroscope at 400Xmagnification.\n\nThe number of cycles,\n\ncrack lengths, and locations measured when each crack was first\nobserved are shown in Table IV-I.\ninitiation\n\nThe number of cycles to crack\n\nappeared to be of the sameorder of magnitude as the\n\nloading condition,\n\nwith the samestress ratio\n\nand stress level,\n\nexcept for the case of the smallest stress levels at R = 0.5\nand R = -2.0. This result can be regarded as quite consistent,\nconsidering that most fatigue test data have shown a tendency\nto be scattered over a substantially\n\nlarge band. The first\n\nobserved crack lengths varied from I0 to I00 micrometers, since\nthe replicas\n\nwere taken at certain\n\nfixed intervals,\n\nas\n\nmentioned before.\nIn most cases, a single crack nucleated and several other\ncracks appeared sequentially.\n\nIn only three specimens out of\n\nthe 24 tested -- one where Smax= 195 MPaand R = 0.5 and two\nwith Smax= 105 MPaand R = -I.0\ninitiated\ninitiation\n\n-- were multiple\n\nat the sametime. Considering the stress,\n\ncracks\nmultiple\n\nwas expected at the highest applied stress level,\n\nin the case where R = -I.0.\n\nas\n\nBut this was not true for R = 0.5.\n\n51\nMost of the crack nucleations were observed along the bore\nof the notch rather than at the corner. The cases where\ninitiation\n\noccurred at a corner may be attributed\n\nto mechanical\n\ndefects from the machining procedure.\nIt was found that most surface cracks which were initiated\nat the bore of the notch were nucleated at the inclusion\nparticles,\n\nas shown in Figure IV-3. This phenomenon\nwas\n\nobserved in many other experiments [1,3,18,30,31,42,43,52],\nespecially\n\nin commercial aluminum alloys\n\ncalled brittle\n\ninitiation.\n\n[I] and has been\n\nIf the crack is initiated\n\nin this\n\nbrittle\n\nmanner, the plastic zone may be considered quite small\n-3\n(estimated to i0 in [52]). But this estimation is limited to\nthe very beginning of crack initiation.\n\nplastic\n\nAnother estimation of\n\ndeformation at the crack tip\n\n[53] is calculated as\n\nfollows.\n\nr o = 0.002 ( em notch\n\nroot.\n\nat\nto\n\nclearly\nis\n\nalso\n\nthe\nthe\n\nroots\ncrack\n\nshow\nused\n\nthe\nto\n\n102\n\n6. The crack compliances of short surface cracks, obtained\nform COD\ncurves, showa linear relationship with the crack\nlength. The compliances of short through-thickness cracks\nalso vary linearly with crack length (in the direction of\ndepth).\n7. The crack closure load ratios measured for the short\ncracks were in general lower than those predicted for\nlonger cracks. There is only a slight difference for\npositive R-ratios, but the difference is significant\nfor\nnegative R-ratios, where the measured closure ratios for\nthe short cracks were nearly zero or less than zero.\n8. An attempt to explain the difference between the growth\nrates using an effective stress intensity factor range to\naccount for the crack closure was partially\nsuccessful.\nThis approach improved the correlation between long and\nshort crack growth for R = -I.0 and -2.0, but did little\nto explain results for positive R-ratios. Microstructural effects and the plasticity\nof the notch root\nadd to the complexity of this problem.\n\n103\nVl. REFERENCES\nI. Replica Method\n\nA replica\ninterval\n\nof the notch surface is madeafter each cyclic\n\nwhich is specified in Section II,\n\nProcedure. At each cyclic interval,\n\nExperimental\n\nthe specimen is held under\n\na constant applied stress, S = (0.8)Smax, while the replica\ntaken. The replica material is acetylcellulose\n\nfilm,\n\nis\n\nwith a\n\nwidth of 0.034 mm(Item Number 14640, Ernest F. Fullan,\n\nInc.),\n\nwhich is cut into pieces about 8 rmm 30 mm.\nX\nPrior to making each replica,\n\nthe notch surface is cleaned\n\nwith acetone. A piece of the replica material\n\nis held in place\n\nloosely against the notch surface using a metal or glass rod\nwith a diameter slightly\n\nsmaller than that of the notch. A few\n\ndrops of acetone, applied with an injector\n\nor a swab, are\n\nallowed to flow between the film and the notch surface. The\nfilm is then touched lightly\n\nto the notch surface and left\n\nto\n\nadhere and dry for at least five minutes. While the replica\n\nis\n\nin place on the specimen, the surface is checked for flaws such\nas bubbles or other artifacts\nmicroscope with a relatively\n\nusing a low-magnification\nlong focussing length.\n\nOnce dry, the replica is slowly peeled from the specimen.\nBest results\n\nare obtained when the replica\n\nis handled with\n\ntweezers. One of the top corners of the finished\nis chipped away to aid in orienting\n\nthe replica\n\nreplica\n\nfilm\n\nfor analysis\n\nunder the microscope. Each replica\n\nis attached with\n\ndouble-sided tape to a microslide,\n\nlabeled with the number of\n\n113\n\ncycles run at that point in the experiment, and stored in a box\nmarked with the specimennumber. Analysis of the replicas\nthe last replica\n\nto those madeearly in the life\n\nfrom\n\nof the\n\nspecimen permits easy location of the crack.\nOccasionally a replica will\n\nbe twisted or have an\n\nunusually large curvature, making crack length measurements\nless accurate. For this reason, the position\n\nof the crack tip\n\nfrom each replica\n\nshould be marked on a montage of micrographs\n\nfrom a relatively\n\nflat\n\nreplica.\n\nthin metal plate with a slit\nreplica\n\nflat\n\nwhen it\n\nA holder can be madefrom a\n\nat the center; this will\n\nis observed under an optical\n\nkeep the\n\nmicroscope.\n\n114\n\nC.
